< Review>
This place is really nice. It has a romantic ambiance, nice artwork on the walls, the food comes in large portions, and are tasty, so if you are not hungry you may need to take a grab bag home. Some of the dishes are extremely spicy, so if your palate can withstand the heat, go for it! There's a bar, and it's loaded with whatever drink or combination you can think of. The servers are nice and courteous. One of the things I admire the most is that it's an extremely clean environment.</Review>

<user_name>Nilesh Kulkarni</user_name><Time>1620451633402<//Time>< Rating>
1< /Rating>
< text>
This is NOT the same restaurant that closed last year. And am sorry but the food was the worst Indo-Chinese I have had ever.
1. Crispy Chilly Baby-corn: this was not at all crispy and soggy in turn. Taste was blah!
2. Chicken Manchurian: OMG! It seems like a watered version of any food. Literally add 2 glasses of water to turn it into an entree. The chicken was not cooked well - I mean you take a piece, cut it and it is raw in the middle. And No, I didnt ask for a medium rare :)
3. Burnt Garlic rice: i have to say this was exactly as written- burn the garlic until it turns like coal and bitter. No flavor to the rice. I have eaten uncooked rice and that might have tasted better.

I am a big fan of Indo Chinese. But this has caused me to have an aversion. Will wait a few months for friends to provide me a personal review before I try back here.< /text>

<text>Went here for the first time this week.  It's been in the neighborhood for awhile and I am glad we finally went.  Not knowing what to expect our party decided to do their lunch buffet.  Figured it was the best way to try a little bit of everything.  The buffet had a variety of food to try and tho I am not a fan of buffets this one wasn't the typical fare but the Indian Chinese fusion selection.  I enjoyed the tom yum chicken soup and spicy creamy fish out of all the buffet choices.  You can get chicken, meat, and veggie choices.  There was also a nice salad.  It's a nice neighborhood find.  Today we took my dad to Father's Day lunch and ordered ala cart.  The servings are family style so be aware the portions are big.  We took off one order after the waiter told us the size of the entree and glad we pared down because it would have been too much food for our party of 4.  Aside from the food the decor was very nice, clean bathrooms, and the remodel from what I think was the old Chinese place is very lovely.  Staff was very friendly, respectful, and accommodating.  I am glad this restaurant is in the neighborhood!</text><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOyVthYNWsS2kBs98e-pNkQ_QGLiGzihpNjUPPw=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pics>< response>

<Rate>5< /Rate>< review>
Went here for the first time this week.  It's been in the neighborhood for awhile and I am glad we finally went.  Not knowing what to expect our party decided to do their lunch buffet.  Figured it was the best way to try a little bit of everything.  The buffet had a variety of food to try and tho I am not a fan of buffets this one wasn't the typical fare but the Indian Chinese fusion selection.  I enjoyed the tom yum chicken soup and spicy creamy fish out of all the buffet choices.  You can get chicken, meat, and veggie choices.  There was also a nice salad.  It's a nice neighborhood find.  Today we took my dad to Father's Day lunch and ordered ala cart.  The servings are family style so be aware the portions are big.  We took off one order after the waiter told us the size of the entree and glad we pared down because it would have been too much food for our party of 4.  Aside from the food the decor was very nice, clean bathrooms, and the remodel from what I think was the old Chinese place is very lovely.  Staff was very friendly, respectful, and accommodating.  I am glad this restaurant is in the neighborhood!</review>

< Text>
My indo-chinese food craving finally found some satisfaction. Best street noodles, appetizers and soup. Do not miss manchurian and Schezwan dishes here. Schezwan rice was tasty but little dry. Sufficient quantity to share. Lava cake dessert is highly recommended. Quick service, less waiting time and helpful staff. Nice location and ample of parking spots.<//Text>

The issue I see is the insane amount of ecologically damaging trash a business creates with utilizing such a huge amount of single use plastic bottles.

I can't in good conscience go to a restaurant that is doing the equivalent of burning tires for warmth.</Text>

< Text>
The restaurant is known for its Indo Chinese fusion cuisine.  There's plenty of unique creations on the menu from the amalgamation of soy sauce and vinegar with Indian spices and profuse amounts of ginger/garlic/onions/other vegetables.  Must try Manchurian style chicken or cauliflower.  Hakka (thin) noodles are a great accomplishment.  Sweet corn soup is another delicacy.  Lunch is usually served buffet style while dinner is ala carte.  My last few experiences have been mediocre.  The burners under buffet servers were not like, and the food felt cold.  The soy sauce level in food and soups is sometimes very high.  It is a hit or miss place.  But definitely worth a visit once if you have not tried Indo Chinese grub.< /Text>

< review>
Went here and after we were seated, a worker rushes out of the kitchen to the outdoor area because they burnt something on a skillet.  It got kinda smokey to the point that the waitress was coughing.  Strike 1.

The waitress finally took our order after we saw her serve what looked like a poorly plated dessert -- it was the Saucy Lava Cake, but there was no sauce and the ice cream looked like it was scooped with a paddle.  Strike 2.

She finally took our order after apologizing 3 times prior that she'll be right with us.  I ordered Chicken Thai Curry - Yellow Curry.  But I asked what was included with it.  She said a bowl of rice to which I corrected myself and asked "what's in the curry?". She says, "oh you know... stuff... peppers, and - " I interrupted her and said, "are there vegetables, like potatoes?". She looked at me as if I was the idiot between the two of us and she says this, "Oh you probably didn't know this but curry is a general term and isn't specific to one country."  She didn't say it rudely but I don't know why she said it at all.  I just wanted to know if there was going to be onions, carrots, and potatoes in my Thai yellow curry like most Thai yellow curries.  She then asks me if I ever had Indian curry, as my fiancee from India is sitting next to me.  I was kind of annoyed but I tried keeping it together.  My final question for her was if the side of rice will be basmati or Jasmine.  She again looks at me weird and says "Well, I don't know... I've never even heard of basmati rice before.". This is the same person that asked me if I ever had Indian curry before.  I then was irritated but told her it's okay, but to just ask if they have Jasmine rice.  She didn't even bother to ask and just said "we don't have Japanese rice.". And so I asked, "well, what kind of rice do you guys have?". She says, "I don't know... tsk.. California San Diego rice... I didn't even know there was all these kinds of rice." And so, I turned to my fiancee and asked her, "can we go?". And we left.  Strike 3.

I post this review not to steer people away, but hopefully to communicate to the Owner of our awful experience.  Hopefully, when we return, it'll be more pleasant.< /review>

< Text>
3.5 star, but for the service and the new fusion, I would give them 4 stars.

The closest Indo-Chinese  restaurant near san Diego before Inchins Bamboo Garden was in Artesia, Irvine, the place called Tangy Tomato.
Inchins Bamboo Garden is great add too Indian and Chinese cuisine and this is a perfect fusion. I am glad they took this business serious and worked hard on the D√©cor and interior. This place has a fusion touch to it and very classy. The location is very convenient, right in the center of the Mira Mesa mall. Also there are plenty of parking if you come through behind, next to Bowling lanes.

Even though this is first time we are here in this restaurant physically, we have ordered from here several times through Doordash. So, Inchins Bamboo Garden is not new for us, its now our go to Asian fusion food.

Coming to food, we have tasted the following
Sweet Corn Soup: Nothing special about it, on the second thought I would have ordered Tom Yum.
Lotus Root Chips: I love these chips, this would be on my order every time. It is Fried Lotus root, and very crunchy
Lat Mai Kai: The best form of chicken I have tried, better than Chicken 65, loved the onion, chilies, garlic combination. It is dried, perfectly cooked, crispy too. It will be great with Fried rice or just like that.
Chicken 65: I like this, but will not agree this is Chicken 65, this must be renamed to Chicken Manchurian. Chicken 65 must be Dry, crispier with lot of curry leaves.
Burnt Garlic Chili Fried Rice: The best rice item in the menu. If kids are eating, ask them to make it mild. They usually put lot of red chilies flakes. You can make it veggies, chicken, lamb or even shrimp.
Singapore Rice Noodle: Out go to Noodles, thin, angle hair like noodles. Not too spicy, great for Kids.
Lo Mein: Will just say OK, nothing extra ordinary about it, will not order again.
Malaysian Paratha: This is just frozen paratha heated in pan.
Lamb Hot Garlic: This is one item we did not like, bland and Lamb was not completely cooked, also it was runny more than beyond
Dessert: Fried Ice Cream - Vanilla ice cream fried covered in Egg Bread crumbs
Service was flawless, and ambience was too good.
Drinks: They have decent collection of domestic and imported beers. Also have good number of basic cocktails. I tried their New English Amber Brow ale and Mosco Mule, no complains here.
Overall this place is like 3.5 star, but for the service and the new fusion, I would give them 4 stars.

Will update more items, as we go there again.< /Text>

<Time>1451552684436</Time><Review>These guys are known for their egg rolls but I came in here one day to order bun rieu (crab noodle soup) and saw from the menu that it came in different sizes. I wanted to see how big the portions were before deciding which size to buy so i asked the woman behind the counter, "How big is the small portion?" To which she replied sarcastically, "Well, it's smaller than the large size."
I decided to ignore her comment and asked the other worker, "Can I see a sample of your small container?"
I don't know about you but after a long day at work, I'm in no mood for a comment like that. I haven't been back to this place since that day. Their bun rieu sucked and it's not as if there aren't any other places to get decent egg rolls in Little Saigon.< /Review>< userid>

< text>
Hands down best smoke shop in Chico. Staff are always welcoming as if you are part of the family. Family run business, great atmosphere, great music always playing, best prices on glass and novelty's for great quality. Anytime I go in for something and they don't have it the next time I go in they end up having it, they are great at getting what the customer wants. Ehab (E)  is always making jokes he's a very funny guy, and always has great advice for all my smoking needs, he's very knowledgeable as well as his father (Rick). The main reason I LOVE The Dungeon is because of the staff, to be honest every smoke shop has the same stuff in them but for the past 25 years that they've been in business the hospitality and compassion for the customer and their needs are most important. Not a single time have I left The Dungeon in disappointment! DungeonBoysForLife!< /text>

<Time>1430351319455</Time><Rate>1</Rate><Text>I, with all honesty, cannot even give this business a one star rating. My very first visit to this business was on the 28th, April. I went online, and checked out all of the 'headshops' in town, and came to the conclusion that I would go and check out, 'The Dungeon" smoke shop. I went in, looked over the array of merchandise. I was not overly impressed, but hey, for all intents and purposes, there was a plentiful selection. I did not find exactly what I wanted, and therefore compromised, on a rather decent looking, bright yellow pipe, of frosted glass, with a silhouette of, Bob Marley. After using the pipe, I decided to clean it. I took a q-tip, and some hot water and proceeded to clean. As the cleaning proceeded, I realized that the yellow was coming off. After further examination, and a bit more cleaning, I realized that the 'yellow' was not infused within, rather, the inside of the pipe was simply hand painted yellow. I was furious that I was sold not only and inferior item, but also, and item that eventually would have damaged not only my lungs, but my very life. I went back the next day, intent on at least getting an exchange. A friend came along. I was greeted by two men, one, the son of the owner, the other, a large red headed guy. I will admit, that my attitude upon entering was borderline surly, though, I never raised my voice. After explaining the situation, I was bluntly told that it did not matter to them. I bought the pipe, and used it, therefore it was not returnable, and, the son of the owner told me that there would be no exchange either, and to get out of his store. He made it succinctly clear that He did not care about my displeasure, or the quality, ( or lack of ), of the pipe. At this point, not only did I become incensed, but so did my friend. After a bit of attempting to calm the situation,  the large red headed guy became a bit verbally aggressive towards myself, and my friend. We were told to get out, threats of calling the police were made, on both sides, and if we had any more issues, we could bring it up with the father. I returned 2 hours later, as instructed, to not find the father there. The owners son was there, and still, with disdain, he informed me that I was not going to get an exchange or a refund. Suffice to say, at this point, all civility went out the door. I made it clear that at least, an exchange was going to happen. I also made it clear that I knew for a fact that this smoke shop sold drug paraphernalia to minors. After a silence of 5 minutes, I was given a decent exchange. I will never go back to this establishment. It is a prime example of the type of smoke shops that ought to not be in business. I will take my business to, Blaze N J's, or, Dragon Tobacco.<//Text><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< Resp>

< Review>
There are a lot of web developers out there, many with great talent to create websites based on exactly the way you want your website to look.  You write the content, give them a specific look you want, and they create it.

We did this with our first two  websites, and had with mediocre results.  We had low traffic to our site and no engagement.

I was in talks with a third developer.  She wanted to know, yet again, how I wanted my site to look.  I told her this: "I need someone to tell me what my site should look like.  I'm not in the website development business, you are.  Frankly, I don't care if there are purple dancing monkeys on my website...if it makes people respond, then that's what I want."  Her reply?  She can't do the design to make visitors respond, and it'll cost me thousands of dollars to get a company to help me with the research and design.

After doing some homework, I found Tiny Frog.  Their hook for me was that they not only wanted to get people to the sites they create, but they also want them to respond.  What a novel concept!!  So I signed on with them.

At my first meeting with Tiny Frog after signing, there were five representatives in attendance from their company: a web strategist, an SEO specialist, a designer, a project manager, and the CEO.  I immediately felt like I was getting my money's worth and would have a good product.  They each had a role:  the web strategist sought to understand my clients and what would make them respond, not only from a look-and-feel angle but also from a content angle.  The designer worked in harmony with the strategist, while at the meeting, to come up with some design ideas that met those concepts.  The project manager put details to the project timeline and milestones.  And the SEO specialist shared in the strategy by discussing what he will do.  And Mikel, the CEO?  He was there to keep the vision for the site at the center of the meeting.  He participated as needed and yet left his team to be the experts he hired them to be.

The result?  I'm very happy.  For once, it's a site I'm proud of.  More importantly, I think our clients engage with it much more effectively.  We get responses!

Thanks Mikel and team for a job well done.< /Review>

<userid>104046247459191384228<//userid><Name>Lupita Pozos<//Name><Date>1610304317338<//Date><rating>5<//rating>< Text>
Best Tripas!
Good tripas are so hard to come by, and then i found El Palacio Del Sabor. Tripas at other places can be burned, stale, too chewy and soft, or they just dont seem like they were cleaned right.. yuck haha. But the tripas here (as long as you ask for them crispy and well done.. dont forget!) are BOMB.COM. A little greasy sometimes but the best I've come by in San Jose. The taste and flavor of the tripas are on point!  My personal favorite: Burrito with carne asada AND tripas mixed (crispy and well done).< /Text>

I had bought a bunch of things from the Dollar tree for a kids event.  But we didn't end up using a few items.  So reading their policy, I went back to exchange it for something else since it was still new and not used.  They were really nice about it and allowed me to exchange it.  But once I got up to the register, I realized  I had grabbed the wrong receipt.  So there I was with a 5 year old and carrying my 2 year old with no receipt in hand to do this exchange.  Luckily for me, Claudia one of the store employees allowed me to do the exchange without a receipt.  She explained that she will allow it just this one time, which was all I needed.  It was a honest mistake on my part and she was just so amazingly nice about it.  I am truly grateful for her kindness.< /text>
